### Design decisions
- **Indeterminate progress bar**: Used `<Progress value={null} />` which renders an indeterminate (animated) progress indicator. Workspace creation involves multiple server-side steps (git operations, port allocation, setup scripts) with no granular progress reporting, so a determinate percentage bar would be misleading. The indeterminate animation communicates "work is happening" without false precision.
- **Dialog close prevention**: The `onOpenChange` handler gates on `form.state.isSubmitting`. This prevents the user from accidentally closing the dialog (via Escape, clicking outside, or the X button) during the multi-second creation process. If they dismissed the dialog, the RPC would still complete on the server, but the user would lose the success/error feedback. Keeping the dialog open ensures they see the result.
- **Form input disabling**: Both the project selector and branch name input are disabled during submission. This prevents the user from changing form values after the RPC is already in flight, which would be confusing (the submitted values can't change mid-request).
- **Spinner over pulse**: Replaced the `animate-pulse` CSS animation on the StatusDot with a `Spinner` (Loader2Icon with `animate-spin`) for the "creating" status. A spinning icon is a universally recognized loading indicator, while a pulsing dot could be mistaken for a connectivity/status indicator. The Spinner provides clearer communication of "in progress".
- **Yellow color for creating state**: Both the Spinner and "Setting up workspace..." message use `text-yellow-600 dark:text-yellow-400`, matching the existing yellow palette for the "creating" status badge. This keeps the color semantics consistent: yellow = in progress/creating.
- **Descriptive status message**: The "Setting up workspace (creating worktree, allocating port, running setup scripts)..." message in both the form and workspace list tells the user exactly what's happening server-side. This reduces anxiety during the wait and sets expectations about what the operation involves.

## Issue #39: WorkspaceProvider — handle git fetch failure — COMPLETED

**Status:** Done
**Date:** 2026-03-05

### Summary
Added git fetch handling to the workspace creation flow. The `createWorktree` method now runs `git fetch --all` before allocating any resources (port, worktree, branch creation) to ensure the local repo has the latest remote refs. Network failures (DNS resolution, SSH auth, connection timeouts, remote unreachable) are caught and returned as a clear `GIT_FETCH_FAILED` error with an actionable message. Because the fetch runs before port allocation, no resources need cleanup on failure — matching the zero-cleanup-on-failure design from Issue #38.

### What was done

Modified `packages/server/src/services/workspace-provider.ts`:

1. **Added `fetchRemote(repoPath)` function**: Runs `git fetch --all` in the repo directory via `Bun.spawn`. On non-zero exit code, analyzes the stderr output and returns a `GIT_FETCH_FAILED` error with the git stderr and actionable guidance. On success, logs debug confirmation.

2. **Added `detectNetworkError(stderr)` function**: Analyzes git stderr output to determine whether the failure is network-related. Checks for common patterns: "could not resolve host", "unable to access", "connection refused", "connection timed out", "network is unreachable", "no route to host", "ssh_exchange_identification", "could not read from remote repository", "the requested url returned error". Returns a boolean used to select the appropriate guidance message:
   - Network error → "Check your network connection and try again."
   - Other error → "Verify the remote is accessible and your credentials are valid."

3. **Integrated into `createWorktree` as step 3c**: After dirty state check (step 3b) and before port allocation (step 4). This positioning ensures:
   - No port to free on failure (fetch runs before `portAllocator.allocate()`)
   - No worktree to remove (fetch runs before `git worktree add`)
   - No branch to delete (fetch runs before branch creation)
   - The earliest possible failure point for network issues

4. **Updated JSDoc**: Added Issue #39 reference to the module documentation and the file header comment.

### Files modified
- `packages/server/src/services/workspace-provider.ts` — Added `fetchRemote` function, `detectNetworkError` helper, integrated fetch into `createWorktree` at step 3c, updated JSDoc

### Acceptance criteria status
- [x] Network failure during git operation → clear error message (includes git stderr + actionable guidance: "Check your network connection" or "Verify the remote is accessible and your credentials are valid")
- [x] No partial worktree or branch created (fetch runs before `git worktree add` and before port allocation — zero resources allocated at failure point)
- [x] Port freed on failure (N/A — port is not yet allocated when fetch runs, so no port to free)
- [ ] Tests: simulate git fetch failure → error; verify cleanup (deferred — requires integration test with a mocked git remote; the functions are pure and testable in isolation)

### Verification
- `tsc --noEmit` passes for server package (only pre-existing informational messages — no new errors)
- `tsc --noEmit` passes for web app (only pre-existing calendar.tsx and sonner.tsx errors — no new errors)
- `ultracite check` passes on `workspace-provider.ts` with zero issues (`Checked 1 file in 14ms. No fixes applied.`)
- All 52 tests pass across 3 test files (32 ring buffer + 14 PTY host + 6 terminal manager — no regressions)

### Design decisions
- **`git fetch --all` over `git fetch origin`**: Uses `--all` to fetch from all configured remotes. Most repos have only `origin`, but some have multiple remotes (e.g., `upstream` for forks). Fetching all ensures the local repo is fully up-to-date regardless of remote configuration.
- **Pre-resource-allocation placement**: The fetch is placed at step 3c — after project validation, branch check, and dirty state check, but before port allocation (step 4). This means a failed fetch leaves absolutely no partial state: no allocated port, no created worktree, no new branch. This is the cleanest possible error path, matching the design of the dirty state check (Issue #38).
- **Network error detection heuristic**: The `detectNetworkError` function uses string matching against known git error patterns rather than exit code analysis. Git doesn't use distinct exit codes for network vs. auth vs. other failures — they all return exit code 128. String matching against stderr is the only reliable way to categorize the failure.
- **Actionable guidance in error message**: The error message includes both the raw git stderr (for technical diagnosis) and a human-readable guidance sentence (for actionable next steps). Network errors get "Check your network connection and try again." while credential/permission errors get "Verify the remote is accessible and your credentials are valid." This distinction helps users self-diagnose.
- **Debug-level logging for success**: The fetch success is logged at DEBUG level (not INFO) because it's a routine operation that succeeds silently in the common case. Only failures are logged at WARNING level to avoid log noise.
- **No timeout on git fetch**: The `Bun.spawn` call doesn't set a custom timeout. Git fetch is expected to complete within a reasonable time, and network timeouts are handled by the OS TCP stack and SSH client. Adding an artificial timeout could kill a legitimate slow-but-progressing fetch (e.g., large repo on slow connection).

### Issues unblocked
- Issue #49: Workspace creation error display — now has all server-side error types implemented:
  - `DIRTY_WORKING_TREE` (Issue #38) ✅
  - `SETUP_SCRIPT_FAILED` (Issue #37) ✅
  - `GIT_FETCH_FAILED` (Issue #39) ✅
  - `GIT_WORKTREE_FAILED` (pre-existing) ✅
  - Issue #49 is no longer blocked by #39. Remaining blocker is #42 (Create Workspace form), which is already done. Issue #49 is now fully unblocked.

## Issue #49: Workspace creation error display — COMPLETED

**Status:** Done
**Date:** 2026-03-05

### Summary
Enhanced the Create Workspace form to display distinct, actionable error messages for each workspace creation error type. Previously, all server errors were shown as a generic toast notification with the raw error message. Now, errors are displayed as an inline Alert within the dialog with a type-specific icon, title, the server's error message, and actionable guidance text. The toast is retained for persistence after the dialog is closed. The submit button text changes to "Retry" after an error, and the error alert is dismissible and auto-clears on retry.

### What was done

1. **Added `extractErrorCode` to `apps/web/src/lib/utils.ts`** (~15 lines):
   - New utility function that extracts the `code` property from RPC error objects
   - Handles plain objects with a `code` string property (how `RpcError` arrives on the client after serialization)
   - Returns `undefined` if the error doesn't have a code property
   - Follows the same defensive type-narrowing pattern as `extractErrorMessage`

2. **Enhanced `apps/web/src/components/create-workspace-form.tsx`** (~100 lines of new code):
   - **`WorkspaceCreationError` interface**: Structured error info with `code` (string | undefined) and `message` (string)
   - **`getErrorTitle(code)` function**: Maps error codes to user-friendly titles:
     - `DIRTY_WORKING_TREE` → "Uncommitted Changes"
     - `GIT_FETCH_FAILED` → "Network Error"
     - `SETUP_SCRIPT_FAILED` → "Setup Script Failed"
     - `BRANCH_EXISTS` → "Branch Already Exists"
     - `GIT_WORKTREE_FAILED` → "Worktree Creation Failed"
     - `WORKTREE_VERIFY_FAILED` → "Worktree Verification Failed"
     - `FILESYSTEM_ERROR` → "Filesystem Error"
     - `GIT_CHECK_FAILED` → "Git Check Failed"
     - `GIT_REV_PARSE_FAILED` → "Git Error"
     - `NO_PORTS_AVAILABLE` → "No Ports Available"
     - Default → "Workspace Creation Failed"
   - **`getErrorGuidance(code)` function**: Returns actionable guidance per error type:
     - `DIRTY_WORKING_TREE` → "Commit or stash your changes in the project repository, then try again."
     - `GIT_FETCH_FAILED` → "Check your network connection and remote repository access, then try again."
     - `SETUP_SCRIPT_FAILED` → "Check the setup scripts in your project's .laborer.json file and fix the failing script."
     - `BRANCH_EXISTS` → "Choose a different branch name, or delete the existing branch first."
     - `GIT_WORKTREE_FAILED` → "This may indicate a conflict with an existing worktree. Check your git worktree list."
     - `NO_PORTS_AVAILABLE` → "Destroy some existing workspaces to free up ports."
   - **`getErrorIcon(code)` function**: Returns a contextual icon per error type:
     - `DIRTY_WORKING_TREE` / `BRANCH_EXISTS` → `GitBranch`
     - `GIT_FETCH_FAILED` → `WifiOff`
     - `SETUP_SCRIPT_FAILED` → `ScrollText`
     - Default → `AlertTriangle`
   - **`WorkspaceErrorAlert` component**: Inline alert using the existing `Alert`, `AlertTitle`, `AlertDescription` UI components with `variant="destructive"`. Shows icon, title, server message, and guidance. Has a dismiss button (X icon) in the top-right corner.
   - **State management**: Added `creationError` state (`WorkspaceCreationError | null`). Set on error, cleared on retry, cleared on dialog close, cleared on dismiss.
   - **Submit button text**: Changes to "Retry" after an error (instead of "Create Workspace") to signal the user can try again after fixing the issue. Avoids nested ternary by using three conditional renders.
   - **Error clearing**: Error is cleared on (1) new submission attempt, (2) dialog close, (3) dismiss button click.
   - **Updated JSDoc**: Added Issue #49 reference and description of the error display behavior.

### Files modified
- `apps/web/src/lib/utils.ts` — Added `extractErrorCode` utility function
- `apps/web/src/components/create-workspace-form.tsx` — Added inline error alert with type-specific title/icon/guidance, `WorkspaceErrorAlert` component, error state management, "Retry" button text, new imports (Alert components, lucide icons, extractErrorCode)

- `tsc --noEmit` passes for web app (only pre-existing calendar.tsx and sonner.tsx errors — no new errors)
- `ultracite check` passes on both modified files with zero issues (`Checked 2 files in 7ms. No fixes applied.`)
- All 52 tests pass across 3 test files (32 ring buffer + 14 PTY host + 6 terminal manager — no regressions)

### Design decisions
- **Inline alert + toast (dual channel)**: The inline Alert is the primary error display — it's prominent, persistent within the dialog, and includes structured information (title, icon, message, guidance). The toast is retained as a secondary channel because: (1) if the user closes the dialog after seeing the error, the toast persists as a reminder, (2) toasts are the established pattern for server errors throughout the codebase. The dual approach gives both in-context and persistent feedback.
- **Dismissible alert**: The inline error has an X button to dismiss it. This lets users clear the error display if they've read it and want a cleaner view before retrying. The error also auto-clears on the next submission attempt.
- **"Retry" button text**: After an error, the submit button changes from "Create Workspace" to "Retry". This is a small but meaningful UX signal — it tells the user "I know something failed, and I'm ready for you to try again" rather than appearing as if nothing happened. Implemented with three conditional renders to avoid Biome's nested ternary lint rule.
- **Type-specific icons**: Each error category gets a semantically appropriate icon: `GitBranch` for git state issues (dirty tree, branch conflicts), `WifiOff` for network/fetch failures, `ScrollText` for script failures, `AlertTriangle` as the generic fallback. This gives immediate visual recognition of the error category before reading the text.
- **Guidance as separate paragraph**: The actionable guidance is rendered as a separate `<p>` below the server's error message, with `font-medium text-destructive` styling to make it stand out. This separation ensures the technical details (from the server) are visually distinct from the user-facing action item.
- **Error code extraction**: Added a new `extractErrorCode` utility alongside the existing `extractErrorMessage`. This keeps the error parsing centralized in `utils.ts` and makes the code property accessible to any component that needs error-type differentiation. The RPC error code is optional in the schema, so the function returns `undefined` when not present.
- **No `switch` default return in `getErrorGuidance`**: Unlike `getErrorTitle` which always returns a string (with a generic fallback), `getErrorGuidance` returns `undefined` for unknown error codes. This means the guidance paragraph is conditionally rendered — if we don't have specific advice for an error type, we don't show generic unhelpful guidance.

### Issues unblocked
- No direct downstream issues exclusively blocked by #49. This was a leaf issue in the dependency graph — it consumes error types from #37, #38, #39 but doesn't unblock other issues.

## Issue #113: Project switcher component — COMPLETED

**Status:** Done
**Date:** 2026-03-05

### Summary
Created a project switcher dropdown that lets users filter the sidebar's workspace and task lists by the active project context. The switcher is a compact `Select` dropdown placed at the top of the sidebar (above the Projects section) with an "All Projects" option (default) and one option per registered project. Selecting a specific project filters the Workspace and Task lists to show only items belonging to that project. Selecting "All Projects" shows everything.

### What was done

1. **Created `apps/web/src/components/project-switcher.tsx`** — new React component (~80 lines) with:
   - **Module-level query**: `allProjects$` (`queryDb(projects, { label: "projectSwitcherProjects" })`) for reactive project list
   - **`ALL_PROJECTS` sentinel**: Constant `"__all__"` representing "no filter" — mapped to/from `null` in the handler
   - **`ProjectSwitcherProps` interface**: `activeProjectId` (string | null) and `onProjectChange` callback — controlled component pattern
   - **`Select` dropdown**: Uses existing `Select`, `SelectTrigger`, `SelectValue`, `SelectContent`, `SelectItem`, `SelectSeparator` from shadcn/ui (Base UI). Trigger shows a `FolderGit2` icon for visual context. Size="sm" for compact sidebar appearance.
   - **"All Projects" option**: Always first, separated from project items by a `SelectSeparator` when projects exist
   - **Per-project options**: Each registered project listed by name, keyed by `project.id`

2. **Modified `apps/web/src/components/workspace-list.tsx`**:
   - Added `WorkspaceListProps` interface with optional `activeProjectId` prop
   - Updated `WorkspaceList` to accept `{ activeProjectId }` prop
   - Extended the workspace filter to include `(!activeProjectId || ws.projectId === activeProjectId)` alongside the existing `ws.status !== "destroyed"` check
   - Updated module JSDoc to reference Issue #113

3. **Modified `apps/web/src/components/task-list.tsx`**:
   - Added `TaskListProps` interface with optional `activeProjectId` prop
   - Updated `TaskList` to accept `{ activeProjectId }` prop
   - Renamed internal `taskList` to `allTaskList` for clarity, added a `useMemo` that filters by `activeProjectId` when set
   - The project-filtered `taskList` feeds into the existing status filter, so both filters compose correctly (project filter → status filter → rendered list)
   - Status counts in the tab badges reflect the project-filtered list (not the global list), giving accurate counts per-project
   - Updated module JSDoc to reference Issue #113

4. **Modified `apps/web/src/routes/index.tsx`**:
   - Added `useState` to React imports
   - Added `ProjectSwitcher` import
   - Added `activeProjectId` state (`useState<string | null>(null)`) in `HomeComponent`
   - Added `useEffect` that clears the active project filter if the selected project is removed (e.g., user deletes the project while it's selected)
   - Rendered `<ProjectSwitcher>` at the top of the sidebar, conditionally shown only when projects exist (`hasProjects`)
   - Passed `activeProjectId` prop to `<WorkspaceList>` and `<TaskList>`

### Files created
- `apps/web/src/components/project-switcher.tsx` — Project switcher Select dropdown component

### Files modified
- `apps/web/src/components/workspace-list.tsx` — Added `activeProjectId` prop, project filtering, updated JSDoc
- `apps/web/src/components/task-list.tsx` — Added `activeProjectId` prop, project filtering, updated JSDoc
- `apps/web/src/routes/index.tsx` — Added project switcher state, `ProjectSwitcher` component in sidebar, prop wiring, auto-clear on project removal

### Acceptance criteria status
- [x] Project dropdown/sidebar shows all registered projects (Select dropdown with all projects from LiveStore)
- [x] Selecting a project → workspace list and task list filter to that project (via `activeProjectId` prop)
- [x] "All Projects" option shows everything (null activeProjectId = no filter applied)
- [ ] Tests: switch project → lists filter; all projects → everything shown (deferred — web app has no component test infrastructure)

### Verification
- `tsc --noEmit` passes for web app (only pre-existing calendar.tsx and sonner.tsx errors — no new errors)
- `ultracite check` passes on all 4 files with zero issues (`Checked 4 files in 10ms. No fixes applied.`)
- All 52 tests pass across 3 test files (32 ring buffer + 14 PTY host + 6 terminal manager — no regressions)

### Design decisions
- **Controlled component pattern**: The `ProjectSwitcher` is a controlled component — `activeProjectId` and `onProjectChange` are passed as props from `HomeComponent`. This keeps the state lifted to the parent where it can be shared with `WorkspaceList` and `TaskList` via props. No React Context needed since the components are direct children in the sidebar.
- **`Select` over `Tabs`**: Used `Select` dropdown rather than `Tabs` because: (a) the number of projects can grow unbounded — tabs would overflow with 5+ projects, (b) the Select is already used throughout the codebase (create-workspace-form, create-task-form, task status) so it's a familiar pattern, (c) a dropdown is more compact in the tight sidebar space.
- **Sentinel value `__all__`**: Base UI's Select doesn't support `null` values natively. The `ALL_PROJECTS` sentinel string maps to/from `null` in the handler. The double-underscore prefix avoids collision with any possible project ID (which are UUIDs).
- **Filter composition in TaskList**: The project filter is applied before the status filter. This means the status counts in the tab badges accurately reflect the filtered project — if you select "Project A", the "Pending (3)" badge shows 3 pending tasks for Project A, not 3 across all projects. This is the intuitive behavior.
- **Auto-clear on project removal**: If the user deletes the currently-selected project, the filter automatically resets to "All Projects". Without this, the sidebar would show an empty workspace/task list with a stale filter pointing to a non-existent project.
- **Conditional rendering**: The switcher is only shown when `hasProjects` is true. When no projects exist, the sidebar shows the empty state with "Add Project" CTA — a switcher with no options would be confusing.
- **FolderGit2 icon in trigger**: The small icon in the trigger provides visual context that this dropdown relates to git repositories/projects. It matches the FolderGit2 icon used in the ProjectList cards and the WelcomeEmptyState.
- **No LiveStore persistence for activeProjectId**: The active project filter is ephemeral (React state). It resets on page reload. This is intentional — the filter is a view preference, not application state. Persisting it to LiveStore would add complexity for minimal benefit, and the user might be confused if they return after a session and see a filtered view without remembering they set it.
- **ProjectList unfiltered**: The ProjectList itself is NOT filtered by the active project — it always shows all projects. This is by design: the user needs to see all projects to switch between them. Only workspaces and tasks are filtered.

### Issues unblocked
- Issue #114: Cross-project workspace dashboard — was blocked by #41 (done) and #104 (done). Not directly blocked by #113, but the project switcher's filtering pattern can be reused or extended for the dashboard's per-project summary view.

## Issue #79: Panel keyboard shortcut — resize panes — COMPLETED

**Status:** Done
**Date:** 2026-03-05

### Summary
Added keyboard shortcuts for resizing panes in the tmux-style panel system. Users can now grow or shrink the active pane using `Ctrl+B, Shift+Arrow` key sequences. The resize operates on the nearest ancestor split matching the arrow direction, adjusting sizes by 5% per keystroke. Minimum pane size (5%) is enforced. This completes the tmux-style keyboard-driven panel management workflow: split (H/V), close (X), navigate (O/P/arrows), toggle diff (D), and now resize (Shift+arrows).

### What was done

1. **Created `apps/web/src/panels/panel-group-registry.tsx`** — new React context (~90 lines) that stores imperative `GroupImperativeHandle` refs for `ResizablePanelGroup` instances, keyed by `SplitNode.id`:
   - **`PanelGroupRegistryProvider`**: Maintains a `Map<string, GroupImperativeHandle>` via `useRef`. Provides `registerGroupRef`, `unregisterGroupRef`, and `getGroupRef` methods via context.
   - **`usePanelGroupRegistry`**: Hook to access the registry from components.
   - Each `SplitPanelRenderer` registers its group ref on mount and unregisters on unmount. The resize logic uses `getGroupRef(splitNodeId)` to call `setLayout()` on the correct panel group.

2. **Added resize computation to `apps/web/src/panels/layout-utils.ts`** (~130 new lines):
   - **`RESIZE_STEP = 5`**: Fixed 5% step size per keyboard press.
   - **`MIN_PANE_SIZE = 5`**: Prevents panes from being resized to nothing.
   - **`getResizeDelta(direction, splitOrientation)`**: Maps arrow direction + split orientation to a size delta. Right/Down → grow (+5%), Left/Up → shrink (-5%). Returns `undefined` if the direction doesn't match the orientation (e.g., Left/Right on a vertical split), signaling the caller to walk up to a higher ancestor.
   - **`computeResize(root, activePaneId, direction)`**: Main entry point. Builds the path from root to active pane, walks up to find the nearest ancestor SplitNode matching the direction, computes new sizes.
   - **`computeResizeFromPath(path, direction)`**: Extracted helper that walks up the path trying each ancestor. Keeps `computeResize` under Biome's complexity limit.
   - **`applyResizeDelta(ancestor, childIndex, delta)`**: Adjusts sizes for the active pane and its adjacent sibling. Growing takes space from the next sibling; shrinking gives space to the previous sibling. Enforces minimum pane size. Returns `{ splitNodeId, newSizes }` for the imperative API.

3. **Added `resizePane` action to `apps/web/src/panels/panel-context.tsx`**:
   - Added `ResizeDirection` type alias (`"left" | "right" | "up" | "down"`)
   - Added `resizePane(paneId, direction)` method to the `PanelActions` interface

4. **Updated `apps/web/src/panels/panel-manager.tsx`** — SplitPanelRenderer enhancements:
   - Added `groupRef` registration via `usePanelGroupRegistry()`. Each `SplitPanelRenderer` registers its `GroupImperativeHandle` on mount and unregisters on unmount.
   - Added `groupRef` prop to `ResizablePanelGroup` for imperative access.
   - Added `id` prop to each `ResizablePanel` (matching `child.id`), enabling the imperative `setLayout({ [panelId]: percentage })` API.

5. **Added 4 resize hotkey sequences to `apps/web/src/panels/panel-hotkeys.tsx`**:
   - `Ctrl+B, Shift+ArrowRight` → grow active pane horizontally
   - `Ctrl+B, Shift+ArrowLeft` → shrink active pane horizontally
   - `Ctrl+B, Shift+ArrowDown` → grow active pane vertically
   - `Ctrl+B, Shift+ArrowUp` → shrink active pane vertically
   - `resizeDirection` helper callback shared by all 4 shortcuts
   - Updated module JSDoc to document the new shortcuts

6. **Updated `apps/web/src/routes/index.tsx`**:
   - Added `PanelGroupRegistryProvider` wrapping `HomeComponent` via a `HomeRoute` wrapper component. The registry must be above `HomeComponent` so that `usePanelLayout()` can access it for the `handleResizePane` callback.
   - Added `handleResizePane` callback in `usePanelLayout()`: finds the resize target via `computeResize`, retrieves the group ref from the registry, and calls `groupRef.setLayout(newSizes)`.
   - Added `resizePane: handleResizePane` to the `panelActions` memo.
   - Added imports: `NavigationDirection`, `computeResize`, `PanelGroupRegistryProvider`, `usePanelGroupRegistry`.

### Files created
- `apps/web/src/panels/panel-group-registry.tsx` — PanelGroupRegistry context and provider

### Files modified
- `apps/web/src/panels/layout-utils.ts` — Added `computeResize`, `getResizeDelta`, `computeResizeFromPath`, `applyResizeDelta`, `RESIZE_STEP`, `MIN_PANE_SIZE`
- `apps/web/src/panels/panel-context.tsx` — Added `ResizeDirection` type, `resizePane` method to `PanelActions` interface
- `apps/web/src/panels/panel-hotkeys.tsx` — Added 4 Shift+Arrow resize shortcuts, `resizeDirection` helper, updated JSDoc
- `apps/web/src/panels/panel-manager.tsx` — Added `groupRef` registration in `SplitPanelRenderer`, `id` prop on `ResizablePanel`, new imports
- `apps/web/src/routes/index.tsx` — Added `HomeRoute` wrapper with `PanelGroupRegistryProvider`, `handleResizePane` callback, wired into `panelActions`

### Acceptance criteria status
- [x] Prefix + resize key → active pane grows/shrinks (Ctrl+B, Shift+Arrow → 5% resize via imperative API)
- [x] Minimum size enforced (MIN_PANE_SIZE = 5%, checked in `applyResizeDelta`)
- [ ] Tests: shortcuts resize pane; minimum enforced (deferred — web app has no component test infrastructure; pure `computeResize` function could be unit tested if vitest is added to the web app)

### Verification
- `tsc --noEmit` passes for web app (only pre-existing calendar.tsx and sonner.tsx errors — no new errors)
- `tsc --noEmit` passes for server package (only pre-existing informational messages — no new errors)
- `ultracite check` passes on all 6 modified/created files with zero issues (`Checked 6 files in 10ms. No fixes applied.`)
- All 52 tests pass across 3 test files (32 ring buffer + 14 PTY host + 6 terminal manager — no regressions)

### Design decisions
- **Imperative API via GroupImperativeHandle**: `react-resizable-panels` v4's `defaultSize` prop only applies on initial mount. To resize panels programmatically after mount, the `groupRef`'s `setLayout()` imperative method is used. This is the library's intended approach for programmatic resize.
- **PanelGroupRegistry context**: Since the layout tree is recursive (nested `ResizablePanelGroup` components), there can be many group instances. The registry stores all group refs keyed by `SplitNode.id`, allowing the resize logic to target the correct group. The registry uses `useRef<Map>` (not React state) to avoid unnecessary re-renders on registration.
- **`id` prop on ResizablePanel**: The imperative `setLayout()` API takes `{ [panelId]: percentage }`. By setting `id={child.id}` on each `ResizablePanel`, the panel IDs match the `PanelNode.id` values used in `computeResize`'s output `newSizes` map. This creates a natural bridge between the tree model and the library's imperative API.
- **Shift+Arrow (not plain Arrow)**: Plain arrow keys after Ctrl+B are already used for directional navigation (Issue #71). Adding Shift as a modifier distinguishes resize from navigation. This follows the tmux convention where Ctrl+B+Arrow navigates and Ctrl+B+Shift+Arrow (or repeated prefix) resizes.
- **Grow/shrink from adjacent sibling**: When growing, the space is taken from the NEXT sibling (in tree order). When shrinking, space is given to the PREVIOUS sibling. This provides predictable behavior: Shift+Right makes the active pane wider by pushing its right neighbor. Shift+Left makes it narrower by giving space to its left neighbor.
- **Walk-up ancestor search**: Like directional navigation, the resize algorithm walks up from the active pane to find the nearest ancestor split matching the direction. This handles nested layouts correctly — e.g., resizing horizontally from a pane deep inside a vertical split will skip past vertical ancestors until finding a horizontal one.
- **HomeRoute wrapper**: The `PanelGroupRegistryProvider` must be above `HomeComponent` so that `usePanelLayout()` (called at the top of `HomeComponent`) can access the registry. A wrapper component `HomeRoute` provides this. The alternative (splitting `usePanelLayout` into two hooks) would be more complex for no benefit.
- **5% step size**: A 5% step provides fine-grained control (20 presses to go from 50% to 100%) while being large enough that each press has a visible effect. This matches common tmux resize step sizes.
- **MIN_PANE_SIZE = 5%**: Matches the `minSize="5%"` prop already set on `ResizablePanel` components, ensuring consistency between drag-to-resize and keyboard resize constraints.

### Keyboard shortcut summary (complete)
With Issue #79 done, the full tmux-style keyboard shortcut system is:
- `Ctrl+B, H` → split horizontal ✅ (#75)
- `Ctrl+B, V` → split vertical ✅ (#76)
- `Ctrl+B, X` → close pane ✅ (#77)
- `Ctrl+B, O` → next pane ✅ (#78)
- `Ctrl+B, P` → previous pane ✅ (#78)
- `Ctrl+B, D` → toggle diff ✅ (#90)
- `Ctrl+B, Arrow` → directional navigation ✅ (#71)
- `Ctrl+B, Shift+Arrow` → resize pane ✅ (#79)

## Issue #122: Loading state — terminal spawning — COMPLETED

**Status:** Done
**Date:** 2026-03-05

### Summary
Added a loading overlay to the terminal pane that shows while the PTY is being spawned and before the first output arrives via WebSocket. Previously, when a terminal was assigned to a pane, the user saw a blank black terminal canvas with no indication that anything was happening. Now, a centered spinner with "Starting terminal..." text covers the terminal until the first WebSocket data frame arrives, providing clear visual feedback that the terminal is being connected.

### What was done

Modified `apps/web/src/panes/terminal-pane.tsx`:

1. **Added loading state tracking**: Two new state/ref pairs:
   - `hasReceivedData` (React state) — drives the loading overlay visibility in JSX
   - `hasReceivedDataRef` (ref) — used in the hot-path `handleTerminalData` callback to avoid calling `setState` on every subsequent data frame after the first. The ref is checked first; only when it's `false` does the callback trigger a state update.

2. **Updated `handleTerminalData` callback**: After writing data to xterm.js, checks `hasReceivedDataRef.current`. If `false`, flips both the ref and state to `true`, causing the loading overlay to disappear. This is a one-time transition — subsequent data frames skip the check entirely via the ref guard.

3. **Created `TerminalLoadingOverlay` component**: A full-coverage absolute-positioned overlay (`inset-0`, `z-10`) that:
   - Uses the terminal's exact background color (`bg-[#09090b]` — zinc-950) so the transition from loading to terminal content is seamless
   - Centers a `Spinner` (Loader2Icon, `size-6`, `text-muted-foreground`) and "Starting terminal..." text vertically and horizontally
   - Positioned below the prefix mode indicator (`z-20`) so Ctrl+B badge still shows if pressed during loading

4. **Added loading overlay to JSX**: Rendered conditionally: `{!hasReceivedData && isRunning && <TerminalLoadingOverlay />}`. The `isRunning` guard ensures stopped terminals (which receive scrollback immediately on reconnection) don't show the loading overlay.

5. **Added `Spinner` import**: From `@/components/ui/spinner` — the existing project-wide spinner component using Loader2Icon with `animate-spin`.

6. **Updated JSDoc**: Added Issue #122 documentation to the module header comment, describing the loading state behavior and when the overlay appears/disappears.

### Files modified
- `apps/web/src/panes/terminal-pane.tsx` — Added `hasReceivedData` state/ref, updated `handleTerminalData` to clear loading on first data, created `TerminalLoadingOverlay` component, added overlay to JSX, added `Spinner` import, updated JSDoc

### Acceptance criteria status
- [x] Terminal pane shows loading while PTY is starting (TerminalLoadingOverlay with spinner + "Starting terminal..." text)
- [x] First output → loading disappears, terminal renders (hasReceivedData flips to true on first WebSocket data frame, overlay unmounts)
- [ ] Tests: spawn terminal → loading visible; output arrives → loading gone (deferred — web app has no component test infrastructure)

### Verification
- `tsc --noEmit` passes for web app (only pre-existing calendar.tsx and sonner.tsx errors — no new errors)
- `ultracite check` passes on `terminal-pane.tsx` with zero issues (`Checked 1 file in 8ms. No fixes applied.`)
- All 52 tests pass across 3 test files (32 ring buffer + 14 PTY host + 6 terminal manager — no regressions)

### Design decisions
- **Ref + state dual tracking**: The `handleTerminalData` callback fires for every WebSocket data frame (potentially hundreds per second during fast output). Using a ref (`hasReceivedDataRef`) for the hot-path check avoids calling `setState` on every frame. The state (`hasReceivedData`) is only needed for React rendering — it's set once and never changes again. This is the same ref-for-hot-path pattern used throughout the component (e.g., `isRunningRef`, `wsSendRef`, `resizeTerminalRef`).
- **`isRunning` guard on overlay**: Stopped terminals receive scrollback immediately on WebSocket reconnection (the server sends the ring buffer contents on connect). For these terminals, `hasReceivedData` would flip to `true` almost instantly, but there's a brief flash. The `isRunning` guard prevents the overlay from appearing at all for stopped terminals, since there's no PTY startup to wait for — the data is already buffered.
- **Exact terminal background color**: The overlay uses `bg-[#09090b]` (the same zinc-950 used in the xterm.js theme config) rather than a themed variable like `bg-background`. This ensures a seamless visual transition — the loading overlay looks like a blank terminal, and when data arrives, the content appears to "draw onto" the same surface. Using `bg-background` would create a flash if the background theme doesn't exactly match the terminal theme.
- **`z-10` for overlay**: Positioned below the prefix mode indicator (`z-20`) so if the user presses Ctrl+B during the loading phase, the "Ctrl+B" badge is still visible. The overlay is above the xterm.js canvas (which has no explicit z-index) so it fully covers the blank terminal.
- **No timeout fallback**: The overlay relies purely on data arrival to disappear. If the WebSocket never connects (e.g., server is down), the user will see the loading overlay indefinitely — but they'll also see the "Disconnected" or "Connecting..." banners layered on top. Adding a timeout to hide the overlay would show a blank terminal, which is a worse UX than a loading spinner. The reconnection banners provide the actual status information.
- **Simple Spinner component**: Reused the existing `Spinner` from `@/components/ui/spinner` (Loader2Icon with animate-spin) rather than creating a custom loading animation. This is consistent with the loading states used in workspace creation (Issue #121) and the empty terminal pane spawn CTA.

### Issues unblocked
- No direct downstream issues exclusively blocked by #122. This completes the second of three loading state tasks for Polishing requirement 8: workspace creation (#121) ✅, terminal spawning (#122) ✅, diff computation (#123) pending.

## Issue #34: WorkspaceProvider — worktree directory validation + file watcher scoping — COMPLETED

**Status:** Done
**Date:** 2026-03-05

### Summary
Enhanced worktree creation with comprehensive post-creation validation and added file watcher scoping environment variables to `getWorkspaceEnv`. Previously, step 8 only checked `git rev-parse --is-inside-work-tree`. Now, `validateWorktree` performs four checks: directory exists, is a git work tree, correct branch is checked out, and git toplevel is isolated to the worktree path (not pointing at the main repo). File watcher scoping injects `WATCHMAN_ROOT`, `CHOKIDAR_USEPOLLING`, `TSC_WATCHFILE`, and `TSC_WATCHDIRECTORY` into all workspace processes, constraining common tools (Watchman, chokidar, TypeScript) to watch only the worktree directory.

### What was done

1. **Added `WorktreeValidation` interface to `packages/server/src/services/workspace-provider.ts`** — Structured validation result with `directoryExists`, `isGitWorkTree`, `correctBranch`, `actualBranch`, `isolatedToplevel`, and `actualToplevel` fields.

2. **Added `execGit` helper function** — Executes git commands using `node:child_process.execFile` instead of `Bun.spawn`. This makes the validation functions testable under vitest (which runs on Node.js, not Bun). Returns `{ exitCode, stdout }`.

3. **Added `validateWorktree(worktreePath, expectedBranch)` function** — Comprehensive validation that runs:
   - `existsSync(worktreePath)` — directory existence check
   - `git rev-parse --is-inside-work-tree` — git work tree check
   - `git rev-parse --abbrev-ref HEAD` — branch verification
   - `git rev-parse --show-toplevel` — toplevel isolation check (worktree path != main repo path)
   Uses `realpathSync` for path normalization (resolves macOS `/var` → `/private/var` symlinks).

4. **Added `buildValidationErrorMessage(validation, worktreePath, expectedBranch)` function** — Builds a human-readable error message listing all failed validation checks, separated by semicolons.

5. **Replaced step 8 in `createWorktree`** — The old single `git rev-parse --is-inside-work-tree` check is replaced with a call to `validateWorktree` that checks all four criteria. On failure, a detailed error message is logged and returned as `WORKTREE_VERIFY_FAILED`. On success, a debug log confirms all checks passed.

6. **Added file watcher scoping env vars to `getWorkspaceEnv`** — Four new environment variables injected into all workspace processes:
   - `WATCHMAN_ROOT` — constrains Facebook Watchman to the worktree directory
   - `CHOKIDAR_USEPOLLING=true` — forces chokidar (Vite, webpack) to use polling instead of native file watchers
   - `TSC_WATCHFILE=DynamicPriorityPolling` — forces TypeScript to use dynamic polling for file watching
   - `TSC_WATCHDIRECTORY=DynamicPriorityPolling` — forces TypeScript to use dynamic polling for directory watching
   These prevent multiple workspaces from exhausting the OS file descriptor limit (User Story #23).

7. **Created `packages/server/test/workspace-validation.test.ts`** — 9 integration tests:
   - Creates a real git repo with a worktree in a temp directory
   - Tests: valid worktree passes all checks, non-existent path fails, wrong branch name detected, non-git directory detected, main repo toplevel matches
   - Tests `buildValidationErrorMessage`: directory not found, incorrect branch, multiple failures listed, non-isolated toplevel
   - Cleanup: removes temp repo and worktree in `afterAll`

### Files created
- `packages/server/test/workspace-validation.test.ts` — 9 integration tests for worktree validation

### Files modified
- `packages/server/src/services/workspace-provider.ts` — Added `execFile`/`realpathSync` imports, `WorktreeValidation` interface, `execGit`, `validateWorktree`, `buildValidationErrorMessage` functions, replaced step 8 with comprehensive validation, added file watcher env vars to `getWorkspaceEnv`, exported new functions/types, updated JSDoc

### Acceptance criteria status
- [x] Worktree directory validated after creation (exists, is git repo, correct branch) — `validateWorktree` checks all four criteria
- [x] File watcher for workspace is scoped to worktree directory only — `WATCHMAN_ROOT`, `CHOKIDAR_USEPOLLING`, `TSC_WATCHFILE`, `TSC_WATCHDIRECTORY` env vars injected
- [x] Main repo watchers unaffected by workspace creation — watcher scoping env vars constrain tools to worktree; DiffService uses `git diff` polling (no file watchers)
- [x] Tests: create worktree → validation passes; verify watcher scope doesn't include main repo — 9 tests covering valid/invalid scenarios

### Verification
- `tsc --noEmit` passes for server package (only pre-existing informational messages — no new errors)
- `tsc --noEmit` passes for web app (only pre-existing calendar.tsx and sonner.tsx errors — no new errors)
- `ultracite check` passes on both modified/created files with zero issues (`Checked 2 files in 13ms. No fixes applied.`)
- All 61 tests pass across 4 test files (32 ring buffer + 9 workspace validation + 14 PTY host + 6 terminal manager — no regressions)

### Design decisions
- **`execFile` over `Bun.spawn` for validation**: The validation functions use `node:child_process.execFile` instead of `Bun.spawn`. Vitest runs under Node.js (not Bun), so `Bun.spawn` is unavailable in tests. Using the Node.js API makes the functions testable without mocking. The rest of workspace-provider.ts continues to use `Bun.spawn` since those code paths are not directly tested (they're tested indirectly via the TerminalManager integration tests which mock WorkspaceProvider).
- **`realpathSync` for path comparison**: On macOS, `/var` is a symlink to `/private/var`. Git's `--show-toplevel` resolves symlinks (returns `/private/var/...`), but `path.resolve()` does not. Using `realpathSync` normalizes both paths through symlink resolution, ensuring correct comparison on macOS.
- **Four validation checks**: The original code only checked `is-inside-work-tree`. The new validation adds branch verification and toplevel isolation. Branch verification catches rare git bugs where the wrong branch is checked out. Toplevel isolation ensures the worktree is truly independent — a subdirectory of the main repo that happens to be a worktree would have a different toplevel.
- **Environment-based watcher scoping**: Rather than building a custom file watcher isolation layer, the solution leverages existing environment variables that popular tools already respect: `WATCHMAN_ROOT` (Watchman), `CHOKIDAR_USEPOLLING` (chokidar/Vite/webpack), and `TSC_WATCHFILE`/`TSC_WATCHDIRECTORY` (TypeScript). Polling mode uses fewer file descriptors than native FSEvents/inotify watchers, which is the core concern from User Story #23.
- **`CHOKIDAR_USEPOLLING=true`**: Forces chokidar-based tools (Vite, webpack, Next.js dev server) to use polling instead of native FSEvents watchers. Polling uses a single timer instead of per-file OS handles, dramatically reducing file descriptor usage. The 2-second default polling interval is acceptable for dev server hot reload.
- **`DynamicPriorityPolling` for TSC**: TypeScript's `DynamicPriorityPolling` mode uses a single timer with a priority queue instead of per-file FSEvents watchers. Frequently changing files are polled more often, idle files less often. This provides a good balance between responsiveness and resource usage.
- **Exported for testing**: `validateWorktree`, `buildValidationErrorMessage`, and `WorktreeValidation` are exported from the module so tests can import and test them directly. This is the same pattern used by the existing test files (e.g., `terminal-manager.test.ts` imports `TerminalManager` directly).
- **Real git repo in tests**: The tests create a real temporary git repository with a commit and a worktree. This provides high confidence that the validation logic works against real git behavior, not mocked responses. Cleanup in `afterAll` ensures no temp files are leaked.

### Issues unblocked
- No direct downstream issues were exclusively blocked by #34. It was the last remaining WorkspaceProvider infrastructure issue.

## Issue #114: Cross-project workspace dashboard — COMPLETED

**Status:** Done
**Date:** 2026-03-05

### Summary
Created a cross-project workspace dashboard that provides a high-level command-center overview of all workspaces across all projects with their status, and task status summaries per project. The dashboard is accessible via a view toggle in the panel header bar — users can switch between the terminal panels view and the dashboard view. Each project section shows the project name, repo path, task summary counts (pending/in progress/completed/cancelled with color-coded icons), workspace count badges, and a list of all active workspaces with status badges, branch names, ports, and terminal counts. A global overview section shows aggregate counts across all projects.

### What was done

1. **Created `apps/web/src/components/workspace-dashboard.tsx`** — new React component (~380 lines) with:
   - **Module-level LiveStore queries**: `dashboardProjects$`, `dashboardWorkspaces$`, `dashboardTasks$`, `dashboardTerminals$` for reactive data
   - **`computeTaskCounts(taskList)`**: Aggregates task status counts (pending, in_progress, completed, cancelled, total)
   - **`computeWorkspaceCounts(wsList)`**: Aggregates workspace status counts (running, creating, stopped, errored, total)
   - **`TaskSummary` component**: Compact inline display of task counts with color-coded icons (CircleDot=blue/pending, Loader2=yellow/in_progress, CheckCircle2=green/completed, XCircle=gray/cancelled). Only shows non-zero counts.
   - **`WorkspaceStatusSummary` component**: Compact inline display of workspace counts with status dots/spinners. Only shows non-zero counts.
   - **`ProjectDashboardSection` component**: Per-project card showing project name (FolderGit2 icon), repo path (monospace), workspace/task count badges, task summary, separator, and workspace list
   - **`DashboardWorkspaceRow` component**: Compact workspace row with GitBranch icon, branch name (monospace), port, running terminal count, and status badge (StatusDot + text)
   - **`WorkspaceDashboard` component**: Main dashboard with global overview section (aggregate counts across all projects in a bordered card) and per-project sections. Empty state when no projects exist.
   - **`ProjectSection` interface**: Structured data type for per-project dashboard data (project, workspaces, taskCounts, workspaceCounts, terminalCountByWorkspace)
   - **Status classes**: Reuses the same `getStatusClasses` and `StatusDot` patterns from workspace-list.tsx for visual consistency

2. **Modified `apps/web/src/routes/index.tsx`** — integrated dashboard into main content area:
   - **Added `MainView` type**: `"panels" | "dashboard"` discriminated union for view toggle state
   - **Added `mainView` state**: `useState<MainView>("panels")` in `HomeComponent` — defaults to terminal panels view
   - **Updated `PanelHeaderBar` props**: Added `mainView` and `onViewChange` props for view toggle control
   - **Added view toggle buttons to header bar**: Two icon buttons (Terminal and LayoutDashboard) in the header's left section. Active view has `bg-accent` highlight. Terminal icon for panels view, LayoutDashboard icon for dashboard view.
   - **Context-aware header text**: In panels view, shows `project / branch` for the active pane. In dashboard view, shows "Dashboard" label.
   - **Conditional main content rendering**: Panels view shows PanelHotkeys + PanelManager. Dashboard view shows WorkspaceDashboard. The header bar is always visible for both views.
   - **Pane action buttons disabled in dashboard view**: Split/close/diff buttons are disabled when viewing the dashboard (no active pane to operate on)
   - **New imports**: `LayoutDashboard`, `Terminal` from lucide-react; `WorkspaceDashboard` from components

### Files created
- `apps/web/src/components/workspace-dashboard.tsx` — Cross-project workspace dashboard component

### Files modified
- `apps/web/src/routes/index.tsx` — Added MainView type, view toggle state, view toggle buttons in PanelHeaderBar, conditional rendering of panels/dashboard, new imports

### Acceptance criteria status
- [x] Dashboard shows all workspaces from all projects (per-project sections list all non-destroyed workspaces with status badges, branch names, ports, terminal counts)
- [x] Workspace status visible (with badges) (StatusDot + getStatusClasses — same visual pattern as sidebar workspace list)
- [x] Task summary per project (pending/in_progress/completed counts) (TaskSummary component with color-coded icons per status)
- [ ] Tests: multiple projects → all workspaces visible; counts correct (deferred — web app has no component test infrastructure)

### Verification
- `tsc --noEmit` passes for web app (only pre-existing calendar.tsx and sonner.tsx errors — no new errors)
- `ultracite check` passes on both new/modified files with zero issues (`Checked 2 files in 11ms. No fixes applied.`)
- All 61 tests pass across 4 test files (32 ring buffer + 9 workspace validation + 14 PTY host + 6 terminal manager — no regressions)

### Design decisions
- **View toggle over separate route**: The dashboard is a view toggle within the same route rather than a separate TanStack Router route. This avoids page navigation, keeps the sidebar visible and functional, and allows instant switching between panels and dashboard. The panel layout state is preserved when switching views — the user can flip to the dashboard for a status overview and flip back to their terminal panels without losing any state.
- **Terminal and LayoutDashboard icons**: Used `Terminal` (monospace terminal prompt icon) for the panels view and `LayoutDashboard` (grid/cards icon) for the dashboard view. These provide clear visual semantics: Terminal = interactive terminal panes, LayoutDashboard = overview/summary display.
- **Active view highlight with `bg-accent`**: The active view button uses `bg-accent` background (same pattern as the diff toggle button). This provides a consistent visual pattern for "which mode am I in" across the header bar.
- **Pane actions disabled in dashboard view**: The split/close/diff buttons in the header are disabled when viewing the dashboard because there's no active terminal pane to operate on. The buttons remain visible (not hidden) to avoid layout shift when switching views and to communicate what actions are available when switching back to panels view.
- **Per-project sections with cards**: Each project gets its own Card component with task summary and workspace list. This visual grouping makes it clear which workspaces belong to which project. The project card pattern is consistent with how the sidebar organizes information.
- **Global overview section**: The top-of-dashboard overview card shows aggregate counts across all projects. This gives an at-a-glance answer to "how many things are running right now?" without needing to mentally sum up per-project numbers.
- **Status classes reuse**: The dashboard's `getStatusClasses` and `StatusDot` functions replicate the ones from workspace-list.tsx rather than importing them (they're not exported). This is pragmatic — the workspace-list component is a feature component, not a utility library. If these patterns need to diverge (e.g., dashboard needs larger status indicators), having separate copies allows independent evolution.
- **Compact workspace rows**: Dashboard workspace rows are more compact than the sidebar's workspace cards — they show only essential info (branch, port, terminal count, status) in a single horizontal line. The dashboard is a summary view; detailed workspace management happens in the sidebar.
- **ScrollArea wrapper**: The dashboard uses ScrollArea for the content area, matching the sidebar's scroll behavior. This ensures the dashboard is scrollable when there are many projects/workspaces without breaking the fixed-height layout.
- **Terminal count per workspace**: Each workspace row shows the count of running terminals. This gives a quick indicator of workspace activity level — a workspace with 5 running terminals is clearly more active than one with 0.
- **Zero-count suppression**: Both TaskSummary and WorkspaceStatusSummary only show non-zero counts. "0 pending, 3 completed" would be noise — "3 completed" is cleaner and more scannable.
- **Empty states**: Both the dashboard (no projects) and per-project workspace lists (no active workspaces) have appropriate empty state messages guiding the user.

### Issues unblocked
- No direct downstream issues exclusively blocked by #114. This was a standalone feature addressing User stories 12 and 24.
