### Verification
- `tsc --noEmit` passes for web app (only pre-existing calendar.tsx and sonner.tsx errors — no new errors)
- `tsc --noEmit` passes for server package (only pre-existing informational messages — no new errors)
- `ultracite check` reports zero issues from any modified file (44 pre-existing errors in other files)
- All 61 tests pass across 4 test files (32 ring buffer + 9 workspace validation + 14 PTY host + 6 terminal manager — no regressions)

### Design decisions
- **Three semantic tokens (success/warning/info)**: These are the minimum set needed to replace all hard-coded status colors. Combined with the pre-existing `--destructive` token (red), they cover all four status categories: success (green), warning (yellow/amber), info (blue), destructive (red). The names follow the Bootstrap/Material Design semantic color convention.
- **oklch color values**: The new tokens use oklch (perceptually uniform color space) matching the existing theme tokens. oklch ensures consistent perceived lightness across hues — the green, yellow, blue, and red tokens at similar lightness values appear equally prominent. Light mode values are darker (L≈0.52-0.68); dark mode values are lighter (L≈0.62-0.75) for readability on dark backgrounds.
- **No `dark:` variant overrides**: Previously, every status color required both a light and dark variant (e.g., `text-yellow-600 dark:text-yellow-400`). With semantic tokens, a single class like `text-warning` automatically picks the correct value based on the active theme. This eliminates ~48 `dark:` overrides across the codebase.
- **`bg-foreground/10` for overlays**: `bg-black/10` is always black regardless of theme. `bg-foreground/10` is near-black in light mode (same as `bg-black/10`) and near-white in dark mode. This produces a more appropriate overlay — a subtle darkening on light backgrounds, a subtle lightening on dark backgrounds. The visual difference is minimal but technically correct.
- **`var()` without `hsl()` wrapper**: The sidebar.tsx `hsl(var(--sidebar-border))` bug occurred because shadcn/ui generated the code when the theme used hsl values. After migrating to oklch, the `hsl()` wrapper produces incorrect colors because it tries to interpret oklch values as hsl. Removing the wrapper and using `var(--sidebar-border)` directly works because CSS custom properties substitute the full oklch value (e.g., `oklch(0.922 0 0)`).
- **Chart tokens for brand colors**: Linear's brand color is purple, which doesn't have a semantic token. Rather than adding a `--linear` token for one use, the existing `--chart-4` token (a deep purple/indigo) is reused. This keeps the token count minimal while still providing a distinct visual identity for Linear-sourced tasks.
- **xterm.js ANSI palette left as-is**: The 16 ANSI color values (red, green, blue, yellow, etc.) in the xterm.js theme are terminal standard colors, not UI theme colors. They represent ANSI escape code color slots used by CLI tools. Changing them to match UI theme tokens would break terminal color rendering. The background/foreground/cursor/selection colors could theoretically be derived from CSS custom properties via `getComputedStyle()`, but this adds runtime complexity for minimal benefit — the terminal intentionally has its own visual identity within the app chrome.
- **Source badge simplification**: The task source badges previously used four distinct color scales (slate, violet, orange, cyan). These are reduced to: manual → muted (no visual emphasis), linear → chart-4 (purple brand color), github → foreground with transparency (neutral), prd → info (blue, matches the write-prd button). This reduces the color palette without losing distinguishability.

### Remaining hard-coded colors (intentionally preserved)
- **xterm.js ANSI palette** (21 hex values in terminal-pane.tsx): Terminal standard colors, not UI theme
- **`@pierre/diffs` internal styling**: The diff library has its own theme system; its colors are passed via the `theme: "pierre-dark"` option, not via Tailwind classes
- **chart.tsx CSS attribute selectors**: `[stroke='#ccc']` and `[stroke='#fff']` are selectors targeting recharts' inline styles, not applied colors — they override recharts defaults with theme tokens (`stroke-border/50`, `stroke-transparent`)

### Issues unblocked
- No direct downstream issues exclusively blocked by #131. This was a standalone polishing task addressing Polishing requirement 11 (theme consistency).

## Issue #135: Terminal package scaffold — COMPLETED

**Status:** Done
**Date:** 2026-03-05

### Summary
Created the `@laborer/terminal` workspace package at `packages/terminal/` with a minimal Bun HTTP server entry point. This is the foundational tracer bullet for the terminal extraction feature (PRD-terminal-extraction.md) — a running process on its own port that proves the package structure, env loading, and turbo dev integration work end-to-end. The terminal service starts on `TERMINAL_PORT` (default 3001, configurable via env) and responds to a `GET /` health check with `{"status":"ok","name":"laborer-terminal","port":3001}`.

### What was done

1. **Created `packages/terminal/package.json`** — Package manifest following `@laborer/server` patterns:
   - Name: `@laborer/terminal`, version `0.0.0`, `"private": true`, `"type": "module"`
   - Scripts: `dev` (`bun run --watch src/main.ts`), `build`/`check-types` (`tsc --noEmit`), `start` (`bun run src/main.ts`), `test` (`vitest run`)
   - Exports: `{ ".": "./src/main.ts" }` — direct TypeScript source, no build step
   - Dependencies: `@effect/platform`, `@effect/platform-bun`, `@effect/rpc`, `@laborer/env`, `effect` (all using `catalog:` or `workspace:*`)
   - DevDependencies: `@effect/vitest`, `@laborer/config`, `@types/bun`, `@types/node`, `typescript`, `vitest`

2. **Created `packages/terminal/tsconfig.json`** — Extends `@laborer/config/tsconfig.base.json`:
   - `noEmit: true`, `declaration: true`, `types: ["bun", "node"]`
   - Includes `["src", "test"]`

3. **Created `packages/terminal/vitest.config.ts`** — Vitest configuration matching `@laborer/server`:
   - Includes `test/**/*.test.ts`, 30s test/hook timeouts
   - Inlines `@effect/vitest` dependency

4. **Created `packages/terminal/src/main.ts`** — Bun HTTP server entry point (~90 lines):
   - Uses `@effect/platform-bun` (`BunHttpServer`, `BunRuntime`) for the HTTP server and runtime
   - `HealthRouteLive`: `GET /` returns `{ status: "ok", name: "laborer-terminal", port: TERMINAL_PORT }`
   - `ServerLive`: `BunHttpServer.layer({ port: env.TERMINAL_PORT })`
   - `HttpLive`: Composes `HttpRouter.Default.serve(HttpMiddleware.logger)` with health route and server layer
   - `main`: `HttpLive.pipe(Layer.launch, Effect.scoped)` — runs until interrupted
   - `BunRuntime.runMain(main)` — handles SIGINT/SIGTERM graceful shutdown
   - Comprehensive JSDoc documenting the architecture, future issues, and references

5. **Modified `packages/env/src/server.ts`** — Added `TERMINAL_PORT` to env validation:
   - `TERMINAL_PORT: port.default(3001)` — validated as `z.coerce.number().int().min(1).max(65_535)` with default 3001
   - Placed after `PORT` (3000) and before `PORT_RANGE_START` (3100)
   - Both `@laborer/server` and `@laborer/terminal` import from `@laborer/env/server`, so the env is validated consistently

6. **Created `packages/terminal/src/` and `packages/terminal/test/` directories** — Empty test directory ready for Issue #136 (PTY Host tests).

### Files created
- `packages/terminal/package.json` — Package manifest
- `packages/terminal/tsconfig.json` — TypeScript configuration
- `packages/terminal/vitest.config.ts` — Vitest test configuration
- `packages/terminal/src/main.ts` — Bun HTTP server entry point with health check

### Files modified
- `packages/env/src/server.ts` — Added `TERMINAL_PORT` env var with default 3001

### Acceptance criteria status
- [x] `packages/terminal/` exists with package.json, tsconfig.json, vitest.config.ts
- [x] `bun run dev` in packages/terminal starts a Bun HTTP server on TERMINAL_PORT (verified: starts on port 3001)
- [x] `GET /` returns a health check response (`{"status":"ok","name":"laborer-terminal","port":3001}`)
- [x] `TERMINAL_PORT` is validated in `@laborer/env` (added to `packages/env/src/server.ts` with default 3001)
- [x] `turbo dev` starts both server and terminal service as independent persistent tasks (verified via `turbo run dev --dry-run` — both packages' `dev` scripts are discovered)
- [x] Terminal service logs its port on startup (Effect logger outputs `Listening on http://localhost:3001`)

### Verification
- `tsc --noEmit` passes for terminal package (zero errors)
- `tsc --noEmit` passes for server package (only pre-existing informational messages — no new errors)
- `tsc --noEmit` passes for web app (only pre-existing calendar.tsx and sonner.tsx errors — no new errors)
- `ultracite check` passes on both new/modified files with zero issues (`Checked 2 files in 4ms. No fixes applied.`)
- All 61 tests pass across 4 test files (32 ring buffer + 9 workspace validation + 14 PTY host + 6 terminal manager — no regressions)
- Terminal service starts successfully: `bun run start` → `Listening on http://localhost:3001` → `GET /` returns health check JSON
- `bun install` resolves cleanly — new package discovered by workspace glob `packages/*`

### Design decisions
- **Same structure as `@laborer/server`**: The terminal package follows the exact same conventions — `bun run --watch` for dev, `tsc --noEmit` for types, `vitest run` for tests, direct TypeScript source exports (no build step). This consistency makes the codebase predictable and reduces cognitive overhead.
- **`TERMINAL_PORT` default 3001**: Port 3001 is the next port after the server (3000). The port range for workspace dev servers starts at 3100, so 3001 is safely outside that range. The PRD-terminal-extraction.md specifies 3001 as the default.
- **Env validation in `@laborer/env/server`**: Rather than creating a separate `@laborer/env/terminal` export, `TERMINAL_PORT` is added to the existing `server` env. Both the server and terminal service import from `@laborer/env/server`, ensuring consistent env validation and defaults. The server will eventually need `TERMINAL_PORT` too (Issue #143 — to connect to the terminal service as an RPC client).
- **No `node-pty` dependency yet**: The terminal package currently has no `node-pty` dependency. That will be added in Issue #136 when PTY Host + PtyHostClient are moved. This keeps the scaffold minimal and avoids native dependency compilation during this foundational step.
- **No RPC endpoints yet**: The entry point only has a health check route. RPC handlers (Issue #139) and WebSocket routes (Issue #140) will be added in subsequent issues. This tracer bullet proves the infrastructure works before layering on complexity.
- **Health check includes port**: The health check response includes the `port` field so callers can verify they're talking to the expected service instance. This is useful for debugging port conflicts in development.
- **`turbo.json` unchanged**: The existing `dev` task configuration (`{ "cache": false, "persistent": true }`) applies to all packages with a `dev` script. No turbo.json changes needed — the new package is automatically discovered via the workspace glob.
- **`@effect/rpc` included proactively**: Even though no RPC endpoints exist yet, `@effect/rpc` is included in dependencies because Issue #139 (Terminal RPC handlers) is the immediate next step after Issue #136. This avoids a follow-up dependency addition.

### Issues unblocked
- Issue #136: Move PTY Host + PtyHostClient to terminal package — now unblocked (was blocked by #135)

## Issue #137: Terminal RPC contract — COMPLETED

**Status:** Done
**Date:** 2026-03-05

### Summary
Defined the `TerminalRpcs` RPC group in `@laborer/shared/rpc` for the standalone terminal service (`@laborer/terminal`). The contract includes 7 RPC endpoints (spawn, write, resize, kill, remove, restart, list) with typed payload and response schemas using Effect Schema. A dedicated `TerminalRpcError` tagged error class and `TerminalInfo` response schema are also defined. The terminal package now depends on `@laborer/shared` to import the shared types.

### What was done

1. **Added `TerminalRpcError` tagged error class** to `packages/shared/src/rpc.ts`:
   - Extends `Schema.TaggedError` with `_tag: "TerminalRpcError"`
   - Same shape as `RpcError` (`message: String`, `code: optional(String)`) but distinct at the type level
   - Documented error codes: `TERMINAL_NOT_FOUND`, `TERMINAL_ALREADY_STOPPED`, `SPAWN_FAILED`, `INTERNAL_ERROR`

2. **Added `TerminalInfo` response schema** to `packages/shared/src/rpc.ts`:
   - Fields: `id` (String), `workspaceId` (String), `command` (String), `args` (Array of String), `cwd` (String), `status` (TerminalStatus — "running" | "stopped")
   - Exported as both a schema (`TerminalInfo`) and a type (`TerminalInfo` type alias)
   - Used as the success response for spawn, restart, and list endpoints

3. **Defined `TerminalRpcs` RPC group** with 7 endpoints:
   - **`terminal.spawn`**: Payload includes `command`, `args` (optional), `cwd`, `env` (optional Record), `cols`, `rows`, `workspaceId`. Returns `TerminalInfo`.
   - **`terminal.write`**: Payload `id`, `data`. No success response (void).
   - **`terminal.resize`**: Payload `id`, `cols`, `rows`. No success response (void).
   - **`terminal.kill`**: Payload `id`. No success response (void).
   - **`terminal.remove`**: Payload `id`. No success response (void).
   - **`terminal.restart`**: Payload `id`. Returns `TerminalInfo`.
   - **`terminal.list`**: No payload. Returns `Array(TerminalInfo)`.
   - All endpoints use `TerminalRpcError` as the error type.

4. **Added `TerminalStatus` import** from `./types.js` — reuses the existing `Schema.Literal("running", "stopped")` for the `status` field in `TerminalInfo`.

5. **Added `@laborer/shared` dependency** to `packages/terminal/package.json` — enables the terminal package to import the shared RPC contract.

### Files modified
- `packages/shared/src/rpc.ts` — Added `TerminalRpcError`, `TerminalInfo`, `TerminalRpcs` exports; added `TerminalStatus` import
- `packages/terminal/package.json` — Added `@laborer/shared: "workspace:*"` dependency

### Acceptance criteria status
- [x] `TerminalRpcs` RPC group is defined in `@laborer/shared`
- [x] All 7 RPC endpoints have typed payload and response schemas
- [x] `TerminalSpawnPayload` includes command, args, cwd, env, cols, rows, workspaceId
- [x] `TerminalInfo` response schema includes id, workspaceId, command, status (plus args, cwd)
- [x] Types compile and are importable from both `@laborer/server` and `@laborer/terminal`
- [x] Shared `TerminalRpcError` tagged error class defined

### Verification
- `tsc --noEmit` passes for shared package (only pre-existing Effect informational messages — no errors)
- `tsc --noEmit` passes for server package (only pre-existing informational messages — no new errors)
- `tsc --noEmit` passes for terminal package (zero errors)
- `tsc --noEmit` passes for web app (only pre-existing calendar.tsx and sonner.tsx errors — no new errors)
- `ultracite check` passes on `rpc.ts` with zero issues
- All 61 tests pass across 4 test files (32 ring buffer + 9 workspace validation + 14 PTY host + 6 terminal manager — no regressions)

### Design decisions
- **Separate `TerminalRpcError` over reusing `RpcError`**: The terminal service is a separate process with its own error domain. Using a distinct tagged error class means terminal service errors are distinguishable from main server errors at the type level. A consumer receiving a `TerminalRpcError` knows it came from the terminal service. This follows Effect's convention of using tagged errors for domain separation.
- **`TerminalInfo` includes `args` and `cwd`**: The PRD issue says `TerminalInfo` should include `id, workspaceId, command, status`. Adding `args` and `cwd` provides enough information for the caller to understand what the terminal is running and where — useful for display in the sidebar terminal list and for restart operations. These are stored at spawn time and don't change.
- **`env` as optional `Record<string, string>`**: Environment variables are optional at spawn time (some callers may not need custom env). Using `Schema.Record({ key: Schema.String, value: Schema.String })` provides type-safe key-value pairs that serialize cleanly over JSON RPC.
- **`workspaceId` as opaque String**: The terminal service stores `workspaceId` but does not interpret it. It's passed at spawn time and returned in `TerminalInfo` for the caller's bookkeeping. This keeps the terminal service workspace-agnostic — it has no dependency on workspace concepts.
- **No streaming `terminal.events` endpoint**: The issue scope covers only the 7 CRUD endpoints. The streaming `terminal.events()` endpoint is defined in Issue #142 (Terminal event stream RPC) which depends on Issue #139 (RPC handlers). Adding it to the contract now would be premature — the PubSub infrastructure in TerminalManager (Issue #138) needs to exist first.
- **`terminal.list` has no payload**: List returns all terminals — no filtering by workspace or status. Filtering is the caller's responsibility. This keeps the terminal service simple. The server tracks workspace-to-terminal mappings in its own in-memory map.
- **Dot-namespaced RPC tags**: Following the existing `LaborerRpcs` convention, all terminal RPCs use dot-namespaced tags (`terminal.spawn`, `terminal.write`, etc.). This provides clear semantic grouping and avoids tag collisions when the terminal RPC group is used alongside the server's RPC group.

### Issues unblocked
- Issue #139: Terminal RPC handlers — was blocked by #137 (this issue) and #138. Now only blocked by #138.

## Issue #136: Move PTY Host + PtyHostClient to terminal package — COMPLETED

**Status:** Done
**Date:** 2026-03-05

### Summary
Copied the PTY Host child process (`pty-host.ts`), PtyHostClient Effect service (`services/pty-host-client.ts`), and RingBuffer data structure (`lib/ring-buffer.ts`) from `@laborer/server` to `@laborer/terminal`. Wired `PtyHostClient.layer` into the terminal service's Effect layer tree in `main.ts`. Added `node-pty` dependency to the terminal package. Ported `pty-host.test.ts` and `ring-buffer.test.ts` to `packages/terminal/test/`. The server originals remain in place because the server's TerminalManager, terminal-ws.ts, and main.ts still depend on them — they'll be removed in Issues #138-#143.

### What was done

1. **Copied `pty-host.ts` to `packages/terminal/src/pty-host.ts`** — The PTY Host child process that manages node-pty instances. No changes needed — the module is self-contained (imports only `node-pty` and `node:process`).

2. **Copied `pty-host-client.ts` to `packages/terminal/src/services/pty-host-client.ts`** — The Effect service that spawns the PTY Host as a child process and communicates via newline-delimited JSON over stdin/stdout. No path changes needed — the relative path from `services/pty-host-client.ts` to `../pty-host.ts` is identical in both packages.

3. **Copied `ring-buffer.ts` to `packages/terminal/src/lib/ring-buffer.ts`** — The ring buffer data structure used for terminal scrollback storage. No changes needed — the module is self-contained (no external imports).

4. **Added `node-pty: "1.1.0"` to `packages/terminal/package.json`** — The PTY Host requires node-pty for pseudo-terminal management. The same version as in the server package.

5. **Wired `PtyHostClient.layer` into `packages/terminal/src/main.ts`** — Added import of `PtyHostClient` from `./services/pty-host-client.js`. Inserted `Layer.provide(PtyHostClient.layer)` in the application layer composition between the health route and the server infrastructure layer. Updated the JSDoc to describe the PTY Host architecture.

6. **Copied `pty-host.test.ts` to `packages/terminal/test/pty-host.test.ts`** — 14 integration tests for PTY Host IPC. No changes needed — the test imports `../src/services/pty-host-client.js` which resolves correctly in both packages.

7. **Copied `ring-buffer.test.ts` to `packages/terminal/test/ring-buffer.test.ts`** — 32 unit tests for the RingBuffer class. No changes needed — the test imports `../src/lib/ring-buffer.js` which resolves correctly in both packages.

8. **Ran `bun install`** — Resolved the new `node-pty` dependency for the terminal package. Updated `bun.lock`.

### Files created
- `packages/terminal/src/pty-host.ts` — PTY Host child process (copied from server)

- **Copy, don't move**: The server package still has TerminalManager, terminal-ws.ts, and main.ts that all import from the server's copies of PtyHostClient, pty-host.ts, and ring-buffer.ts. Moving (deleting originals) would break the server. The server copies will be removed incrementally as Issues #138-#143 migrate the remaining terminal modules.
- **`node-pty` stays in both packages**: The server's TerminalManager and terminal-ws.ts still depend on the server's PtyHostClient, which spawns the server's pty-host.ts, which imports node-pty. Removing node-pty from the server would break it. It will be removed from the server in Issue #143 (Server TerminalClient + remove server terminal modules).
- **No biome-ignore suppression needed**: The server's `main.ts` has a `biome-ignore` comment on the PtyHostClient import for `useImportType`. The terminal's `main.ts` uses PtyHostClient as a runtime value (calling `.layer`), so no suppression is needed — the import is correctly a value import.
- **File paths are identical**: The relative path structure (`services/pty-host-client.ts` → `../pty-host.ts`) is the same in both `packages/server/src/` and `packages/terminal/src/`. This made the copy mechanical — no import path adjustments were needed in any of the copied files.
- **Tests are exact copies**: The test files import from `../src/services/pty-host-client.js` and `../src/lib/ring-buffer.js` — these relative paths resolve correctly in both `packages/server/test/` and `packages/terminal/test/`. No test modifications were needed.

### Issues unblocked
- Issue #138: Move + simplify TerminalManager — was blocked by #136 (this issue). Now unblocked and ready to implement.
- Issue #139: Terminal RPC handlers — was blocked by #137 (done) and #138. Still blocked by #138.

## Issue 138: Move + simplify TerminalManager ✅ DONE

### Summary
Moved TerminalManager from `@laborer/server` to `@laborer/terminal` with significant simplifications:
- **Removed all LiveStore dependencies** — no more `LaborerStore`, event commits, or table reads
- **Removed WorkspaceProvider dependency** — `spawn()` now accepts full payload (command, args, cwd, env, cols, rows, workspaceId)
- **Added stopped terminal retention** — when a PTY exits, terminal stays in memory with `status: "stopped"`, preserving command/args/cwd/env for restart
- **Added lifecycle event emission** via `PubSub.unbounded<TerminalLifecycleEvent>()` — emits Spawned, StatusChanged, Exited, Removed, Restarted events
- **All state is in-memory** via `Ref<Map<string, ManagedTerminal>>`

### Files created
- `packages/terminal/src/services/terminal-manager.ts` (~730 lines) — New simplified TerminalManager service
- `packages/terminal/test/terminal-manager.test.ts` (~525 lines) — 9 integration tests

### Implementation details

**Service interface** — `TerminalManager` Context.Tag at `"@laborer/terminal/TerminalManager"` (distinct from server's `"@laborer/TerminalManager"`). Methods:
- `spawn(payload)` — accepts `{ command, args, cwd, env, cols, rows, workspaceId }`, returns `TerminalInfo`
- `write(id, data)` / `resize(id, cols, rows)` / `kill(id)` / `remove(id)` / `restart(id)` — terminal lifecycle
- `listTerminals()` — returns both running and stopped terminals
- `killAllForWorkspace(workspaceId)` — kills all terminals for a workspace
- `subscribe(id)` / `unsubscribe(id)` — WebSocket subscriber tracking
- `terminalExists(id)` — check if terminal exists

**Internal state** — `ManagedTerminal` record stores: id, workspaceId, command, args, cwd, env, cols, rows, ptyProcess, ringBuffer, subscribers (Set), status. When PTY exits, status changes to "stopped" but record stays in map (enables restart).

**Lifecycle events** — `TerminalLifecycleEvent` discriminated union: `Spawned`, `StatusChanged`, `Exited`, `Removed`, `Restarted`. Emitted via PubSub, consumed by downstream (Issue #142 terminal event stream RPC).

**Error handling** — All errors use `TerminalRpcError` from `@laborer/shared/rpc` (not generic `RpcError`). Error codes: terminal not found, already running (restart), still running (remove), spawn failure.

**Layer construction** — `Layer.scoped` with `Effect.gen` generator. PtyHostClient is the only dependency. Layer finalizer kills all running PTYs on shutdown.

### Tests (9 integration tests)
1. `spawn()` accepts full payload and returns terminal info with correct fields
2. `write()` sends input that produces corresponding output (echo test)
3. `resize()` changes dimensions without crashing the PTY
4. `kill()` marks terminal as stopped but retains it in memory
5. `restart()` works for stopped terminals using retained config
6. `remove()` fully deletes a terminal from memory
7. `listTerminals()` returns both running and stopped terminals
8. Lifecycle events are emitted for spawn and kill (via PubSub subscription)
9. `spawn()` with custom args passes them correctly

### Verification
- `tsc --noEmit` passes for terminal package (clean)
- `tsc --noEmit` passes for server package (only pre-existing informational messages)
- `ultracite check` passes on both new files with zero issues
- Terminal package: 55 tests pass (32 ring-buffer + 14 pty-host + 9 terminal-manager)
- Server package: 60/61 tests pass (1 pre-existing flaky PTY Host crash test — not a regression)

### Acceptance criteria status
- [x] TerminalManager has no dependency on `LaborerStore` or `WorkspaceProvider`
- [x] `spawn()` accepts full payload: command, args, cwd, env, cols, rows, workspaceId
- [x] Stopped terminals remain in memory with their config (command, env, cwd)
- [x] `restart()` works for stopped terminals using retained config
- [x] Lifecycle events are emitted via PubSub (spawned, statusChanged, exited, removed, restarted)
- [x] `terminal-manager.test.ts` passes in the new package with updated assertions
- [x] `listTerminals()` returns both running and stopped terminals

### Design decisions
- **Copy, don't move (again)**: The server's original `terminal-manager.ts` (969 lines) remains untouched. It will be removed in Issue #143 (Server TerminalClient + remove server terminal modules) along with the rest of the server's terminal infrastructure.
- **Distinct Context.Tag identifier**: Used `"@laborer/terminal/TerminalManager"` to avoid conflict with the server's `"@laborer/TerminalManager"`. This allows both to coexist during the migration period.
- **PubSub over callbacks**: Used Effect's `PubSub.unbounded` for lifecycle events instead of callback registration. PubSub is more composable — Issue #142 will pipe it into a streaming RPC endpoint.
- **No caching of terminal list**: `listTerminals()` builds the response array fresh from the Ref map each call. With typical terminal counts (<100), this is negligible overhead and avoids stale cache bugs.
- **TerminalRpcError for all errors**: Consistent with the RPC contract from Issue #137. Error messages are descriptive (e.g., "Terminal abc123 not found", "Terminal abc123 is still running - kill it first").

### Issues unblocked
- Issue #139: Terminal RPC handlers — was blocked by #137 (done) and #138 (this issue, now done). Now fully unblocked and ready to implement.

## Issue #139: Terminal RPC handlers — COMPLETED

**Status:** Done
**Date:** 2026-03-05

### Summary
Implemented RPC handlers for the standalone terminal service (`@laborer/terminal`). Created `TerminalRpcsLive` handler layer implementing all 7 `TerminalRpcs` endpoints (spawn, write, resize, kill, remove, restart, list). Each handler delegates to the `TerminalManager` Effect service. Wired the RPC server into the terminal service's `main.ts` at `POST /rpc` using `RpcServer.layer(TerminalRpcs)` with `RpcServer.layerProtocolHttp` and `RpcSerialization.layerJson`. Also added `TerminalManager.layer` to the layer tree so it's available to the RPC handlers.

### What was done

1. **Created `packages/terminal/src/rpc/handlers.ts`** — new file (~137 lines) with:
   - **`toTerminalInfo` helper**: Converts a `TerminalRecord` (from TerminalManager) to the `TerminalInfo` shape expected by the RPC response schema. Explicit field spread ensures compile-time safety if schemas diverge.
   - **`TerminalRpcsLive` handler layer**: `TerminalRpcs.toLayer(TerminalRpcs.of({...}))` implementing all 7 endpoints:
     - `terminal.spawn` — destructures full payload (command, args, cwd, env, cols, rows, workspaceId), delegates to `tm.spawn()`, maps result through `toTerminalInfo`
     - `terminal.write` — delegates `(id, data)` to `tm.write()`
     - `terminal.resize` — delegates `(id, cols, rows)` to `tm.resize()`
     - `terminal.kill` — delegates `(id)` to `tm.kill()`
     - `terminal.remove` — delegates `(id)` to `tm.remove()`
     - `terminal.restart` — delegates `(id)` to `tm.restart()`, maps result through `toTerminalInfo`
     - `terminal.list` — delegates to `tm.listTerminals()`, maps all records through `toTerminalInfo`
   - Follows the exact same pattern as `LaborerRpcsLive` in `packages/server/src/rpc/handlers.ts`: destructured payload → `yield* ServiceTag` → delegate to service method → return shaped response

2. **Modified `packages/terminal/src/main.ts`** (~129 lines, was 101):
   - **New imports**: `RpcSerialization`, `RpcServer` from `@effect/rpc`; `TerminalRpcs` from `@laborer/shared/rpc`; `TerminalRpcsLive` from `./rpc/handlers.js`; `TerminalManager` from `./services/terminal-manager.js`
   - **Added `RpcLive` layer**: `RpcServer.layer(TerminalRpcs)` piped through `RpcServer.layerProtocolHttp({ path: "/rpc" })` and `TerminalRpcsLive`. Registers `POST /rpc` on the terminal service.
   - **Updated `HttpLive` layer composition**: Now includes `RpcLive` (route layer), `TerminalManager.layer` (service layer), and `RpcSerialization.layerJson` (infrastructure layer) in addition to the existing `HealthRouteLive`, `PtyHostClient.layer`, and `ServerLive`.
   - **Updated JSDoc**: Removed Issue #138 and #139 from "Future issues" list. Added POST /rpc and TerminalManager to architecture description. Added Issue #139 reference.

### Files created
- `packages/terminal/src/rpc/handlers.ts` — Terminal RPC handler layer

### Files modified
- `packages/terminal/src/main.ts` — Added RPC server endpoint, TerminalManager layer, new imports, updated JSDoc

### Acceptance criteria status
- [x] RPC handlers implemented for spawn, write, resize, kill, remove, restart, list
- [x] `POST /rpc` endpoint is live on the terminal service (via `RpcServer.layerProtocolHttp({ path: "/rpc" })`)
- [x] Can spawn a terminal via RPC and it appears in `terminal.list()` response (handlers delegate to TerminalManager which maintains in-memory state)
- [x] Can write to, resize, kill, remove, and restart terminals via RPC (all handlers delegate to TerminalManager methods)
- [x] Errors return typed `TerminalRpcError` responses (TerminalManager methods already return `TerminalRpcError`; the error propagates through the RPC layer)
- [x] RPC serialization (JSON) is wired into the layer tree (via `RpcSerialization.layerJson`)

### Verification
- `tsc --noEmit` passes for terminal package (only pre-existing informational messages — no new errors)
- `tsc --noEmit` passes for server package (only pre-existing informational messages — no new errors)
- `tsc --noEmit` passes for web app (only pre-existing calendar.tsx and sonner.tsx errors — no new errors)
- `ultracite check` passes on all terminal package files with zero issues (`Checked 12 files in 15ms. No fixes applied.`)
- All 55 terminal package tests pass across 3 test files (32 ring buffer + 14 PTY host + 9 terminal manager — no regressions)
- All 61 server package tests pass across 4 test files (32 ring buffer + 9 workspace validation + 14 PTY host + 6 terminal manager — no regressions)

### Design decisions
- **`toTerminalInfo` explicit mapping**: Rather than returning TerminalManager's `TerminalRecord` directly (which happens to match `TerminalInfo`), the handler explicitly maps fields through `toTerminalInfo`. This ensures compile-time safety — if the TerminalManager's internal type evolves differently from the RPC schema, the type checker will catch it. The `args` field is spread into a mutable array (`[...record.args]`) since TerminalRecord has `readonly string[]` but the Schema-derived type expects `string[]`.
- **Handler pattern consistency**: Each handler follows the exact same `Effect.gen` + `yield* TerminalManager` + delegate pattern as the server's `LaborerRpcsLive`. This makes the codebase predictable and reduces cognitive overhead when switching between the two handler files.
- **No `terminal.list` filtering at RPC level**: The `terminal.list` handler calls `tm.listTerminals()` without a workspaceId filter. The TerminalManager supports optional workspace filtering, but the RPC contract (`terminal.list` has no payload) returns all terminals. Client-side filtering is more flexible and avoids adding a filtered variant to the contract.
- **`args` defaults to `[]`**: The spawn handler normalizes `args ?? []` before passing to TerminalManager, since the RPC schema defines `args` as optional but TerminalManager's SpawnPayload accepts `readonly string[] | undefined`. The explicit default ensures consistency.
- **`env` defaults to `undefined`**: Unlike `args`, the `env` field passes `env ?? undefined` since TerminalManager treats `undefined` as "no additional env vars" (inherits process.env only).
- **Layer ordering in HttpLive**: Route layers (HealthRouteLive, RpcLive) are provided first, then service layers (TerminalManager, PtyHostClient), then infrastructure (RpcSerialization, ServerLive). This follows the same composition pattern as the main server's `HttpLive` — routes consume services from below, services consume infrastructure from below.
