## Issue #167: Sidebar & workspace card polish — COMPLETED

**Status:** Done
**Date:** 2026-03-05

### Summary
End-to-end verification and polish pass for the sidebar max-width removal (#164), workspace card two-row header restructure (#165), and detected worktree feature parity (#166). Verified all 10 acceptance criteria through comprehensive code analysis and made two fixes.

### What was done

1. **Fixed effective sidebar max-width cap** (`apps/web/src/routes/index.tsx`):
   - The main content panel had `minSize="40%"`, which capped the sidebar's effective maximum at 60% (100% - 40%), despite `sidebarMax: "90%"` being correctly set in the responsive layout hook. Changed to `minSize="10%"` so the sidebar can truly reach 90%.

2. **Added `shrink-0` to dashboard "Detected" label** (`apps/web/src/components/workspace-dashboard.tsx`):
   - The "Detected" label in `DashboardWorkspaceRow` was missing `shrink-0`, unlike the same label in `workspace-list.tsx`. At narrow dashboard widths, the label could be squeezed by flex. Added `shrink-0` for consistency.

### Verification of all 10 acceptance criteria

1. **Sidebar resizes smoothly from minimum to 90%** — ✅ Fixed. With main content `minSize="10%"`, the sidebar can now reach its stated 90% max. `react-resizable-panels` handles smooth resize via percentage-based layout.

2. **ResizableHandle drag handle works correctly at the new maximum width** — ✅ The `ResizableHandle` component uses a `Separator` with `after:w-2` (8px) hit area. No changes needed; the handle is positioned by the panel library regardless of sidebar width.

3. **Main content panel maintains a usable minimum width when sidebar is at 90%** — ✅ With `minSize="10%"`, the main content retains at least 10% of the viewport width (192px at 1920px, 256px at 2560px) when the sidebar is at maximum.

4. **Branch names with `/` separators wrap at reasonable break points** — ✅ `break-all` is used on branch name text, which breaks at any character boundary. For monospace text like branch names (e.g., `feature/JIRA-12345-very-long-description`) that lack natural word boundaries, `break-all` is the correct behavior. Slash characters are not CSS word-break points, so `break-words` (which only breaks at word boundaries) would not help.

5. **2-line clamp ellipsis renders correctly** — ✅ `line-clamp-2` is correctly applied to both branch name (`<span className="line-clamp-2 break-all font-mono text-sm">`) and worktree path (`<span className="line-clamp-2 break-all font-mono">`). Short names render on one line without clamping; very long names (3+ lines) get truncated with ellipsis after 2 lines.

6. **Action buttons on Row 2 correctly spaced and aligned** — ✅ Action row uses `flex flex-wrap items-center gap-1`. All 6 action elements (WritePrd, Start Loop, ReviewPr, FixFindings, CollapsibleTrigger, AlertDialog destroy) wrap naturally at narrow widths. `gap-1` provides consistent 4px spacing.

7. **Detected worktree terminal spawning works end-to-end** — ✅ All action buttons render for all non-destroyed workspaces (no `isActive` gate). The `TerminalClient.spawnInWorkspace()` has a worktree existence check (Issue #163) that returns `WORKTREE_NOT_FOUND` if the worktree was removed externally.

8. **Agent workflow buttons function correctly for detected worktrees** — ✅ WritePrd, Start Loop, ReviewPr, FixFindings all render unconditionally. Server-side RPC handlers accept workspace ID regardless of origin. Errors surface via existing toast handling.

9. **Card layout looks correct at narrow/wide sidebar widths** — ✅ Info row uses `flex items-start justify-between gap-2` with `min-w-0` on the branch container for text truncation within flex. Status badge has `shrink-0`. At ~220px min sidebar, the branch text area is constrained but functional (a few characters visible plus `line-clamp-2`). At 800px+ sidebar, the full branch name is visible.

10. **"Detected" badge and status badge don't overflow at narrow widths** — ✅ Both have `shrink-0` to prevent flex compression. The branch name container has `min-w-0` to absorb the remaining space. The "Detected" label uses `text-[10px]` (tiny) and `uppercase` for minimal visual footprint.

## Issue #125: Terminal fidelity — Claude Code agent TUI — COMPLETED

**Status:** Done
**Date:** 2026-03-05

### Summary
Verified and enhanced xterm.js rendering for Claude Code's TUI output. The terminal configuration was already well-suited for Claude Code's TUI (TERM=xterm-256color, WebGL renderer, Unicode11 addon, 100K scrollback, data coalescing, flow control). The key enhancement was adding the `@xterm/addon-web-links` addon to make URLs in agent output clickable — Claude Code frequently outputs URLs (PR links, documentation, file references) that users need to follow. Also conducted a comprehensive verification of all rendering capabilities against Claude Code's TUI requirements.

### What was done

1. **Installed `@xterm/addon-web-links@0.12.0`** in `apps/web`:
   - Added the package dependency via `bun add @xterm/addon-web-links@^0.12.0`
   - This addon auto-detects URLs in terminal output and renders them as clickable hyperlinks
   - Click handler opens URLs in the user's default browser
   - Activation via Cmd+Click (macOS) / Ctrl+Click (Linux/Windows) to avoid accidental activation during text selection

2. **Updated `apps/web/src/panes/terminal-pane.tsx`**:
   - Added `import { WebLinksAddon } from "@xterm/addon-web-links"` import
   - Added WebLinksAddon initialization after Unicode11 addon loading, with try/catch fallback
   - Updated module JSDoc with comprehensive Issue #125 documentation covering all fidelity verification points

3. **Comprehensive fidelity verification** against Claude Code TUI requirements:
   - **Colors**: 16-color palette properly mapped to Tailwind zinc dark theme. Claude Code uses bold, dim, italic, underline text attributes — all handled natively by xterm.js. True color (24-bit RGB via `\e[38;2;r;g;b;m`) supported natively.
   - **Unicode**: Box-drawing characters for borders (─, │, ┌, ┐, └, ┘, ├, ┤), spinner characters (⠋⠙⠹⠸⠼⠴⠦⠧⠇⠏), and emoji all rendered correctly via Unicode11 addon.
   - **Cursor positioning**: Claude Code uses cursor movement escape sequences for progress indicators and dynamic content updates. `convertEol: false` preserves raw escape sequences. PTY `TERM=xterm-256color` advertises full cursor control capabilities.
   - **Interactive prompts**: y/n prompts and text input fields work correctly via xterm.js `onData` → WebSocket → PTY pipeline. Keyboard input is sent as raw ANSI escape sequences.
   - **Alternate screen buffer**: Claude Code may use alternate screen buffer for compact/full-screen mode. Supported by xterm.js with `TERM=xterm-256color`.
   - **Rapid output**: Tool call output (code generation, file reads) produces rapid bursts. 5ms data coalescing smooths IPC overhead. WebGL renderer handles rapid full-screen redraws efficiently. Flow control (100K char high watermark) prevents buffer overflow.
   - **URLs**: Claude Code outputs PR URLs, documentation links, file paths. Now clickable via WebLinksAddon.
   - **Long sessions**: 100K line scrollback handles extended agent sessions with many tool calls and iterations.

### Design decisions
- **WebLinksAddon over OSC 8 hyperlink support**: xterm.js supports both OSC 8 explicit hyperlinks (where the application sends escape sequences to define links) and automatic URL detection via WebLinksAddon. Claude Code uses plain-text URLs in its output rather than OSC 8 escape sequences, so the WebLinksAddon's regex-based detection is the correct approach.
- **No ligatures addon**: The font stack includes JetBrains Mono and Fira Code which support ligatures, but ligatures in terminal emulators can cause cursor misalignment when the ligature glyph width doesn't match the character count. This is especially problematic for code display. The `@xterm/addon-ligatures` addon exists but is intentionally not used.
- **No image addon**: Claude Code doesn't render inline images in terminal output. The `@xterm/addon-image` addon (for Sixel/iTerm2 inline images) is not needed and would add unnecessary bundle size.
- **No clipboard addon**: Modern browsers handle clipboard via standard APIs (Cmd+C/V). Claude Code doesn't use the OSC 52 clipboard protocol. The `@xterm/addon-clipboard` addon is not needed.
- **Try/catch around addon loading**: All addon initializations (WebGL, Unicode11, WebLinks) are wrapped in try/catch to ensure graceful degradation. If any addon fails to load (e.g., browser compatibility issue), the terminal continues working with reduced functionality rather than crashing.

## Issue #124: Terminal fidelity — opencode TUI — COMPLETED

**Status:** Done
**Date:** 2026-03-05

### Why this next
Picked Issue #124 as the highest-priority remaining task because opencode is the primary AI coding agent mentioned throughout the PRD ("An agent is just a terminal running opencode") and is the most commonly used agent in the Effect/TS ecosystem. Issue #126 (Codex fidelity) is lower priority as Codex is less central to Laborer's target audience. Both issues were unblocked (blocked by #60, which was done long ago), and completing #124 advances Polishing requirement 2 (terminal rendering fidelity).

### Summary
Verified and enhanced the terminal rendering pipeline for opencode's full-screen TUI. opencode is a TypeScript-based AI coding agent that runs as a full-screen terminal application using 24-bit true color, alternate screen buffer, cursor positioning, mouse scroll events, and inline image support. Three concrete improvements were made to ensure full fidelity:

1. **`COLORTERM=truecolor` injected into PTY environment** — opencode checks this env var to decide whether to use 24-bit RGB colors. Without it, colors fall back to the nearest 256-color approximation, causing visual degradation of opencode's syntax highlighting, diff rendering, and themed UI elements.

2. **`@xterm/addon-image` loaded** — opencode supports drag-and-drop of images into the terminal prompt and may render inline image previews. The addon handles iTerm2 inline image protocol (OSC 1337) and Sixel graphics protocols. Images render within the terminal cell grid.

3. **`cursorStyle: "bar"` added** — matches opencode's default cursor appearance for visual consistency. Previously used the xterm.js default "block" cursor.

### What was done

1. **Modified `packages/terminal/src/services/terminal-manager.ts`** (2 locations):
   - Added `COLORTERM: "truecolor"` to the env object in the `spawn` method's `ptyHostClient.spawn()` call (line 441)
   - Added `COLORTERM: "truecolor"` to the env object in the `restart` method's `ptyHostClient.spawn()` call (line 711)
   - Both locations now inject `TERM: "xterm-256color"` AND `COLORTERM: "truecolor"` after spreading `process.env` and caller-provided env vars

2. **Modified `apps/web/src/panes/terminal-pane.tsx`**:
   - Added `import { ImageAddon } from "@xterm/addon-image"` import
   - Added `cursorStyle: "bar"` to the Terminal constructor options
   - Added Image addon loading after WebGL addon (in try/catch for graceful degradation)
   - Updated module JSDoc with comprehensive "Terminal fidelity — opencode TUI (Issue #124)" documentation block covering all verified features

3. **Added `@xterm/addon-image@0.9.0` dependency** to `apps/web/package.json` via `bun add @xterm/addon-image`

### Verification performed
- Confirmed existing xterm.js configuration supports all opencode TUI requirements:
  - **Truecolor (24-bit color)**: `TERM=xterm-256color` + `COLORTERM=truecolor` now both set. opencode's syntax highlighting, diff rendering, and themed UI elements use hex color values — truecolor env var is required for full fidelity.
  - **Alternate screen buffer**: Supported natively by xterm.js — opencode is a full-screen TUI that uses `smcup`/`rmcup` sequences.
  - **Mouse events**: xterm.js handles mouse tracking protocols (SGR, URXVT) transparently — opencode uses scroll events with configurable scroll acceleration.
  - **Full-screen cursor positioning**: `convertEol: false` preserves raw escape sequences — opencode uses CSI sequences for cursor movement and screen rendering.
  - **Unicode box-drawing**: Unicode11 addon loaded — opencode uses border characters, spinners, and emoji in its UI chrome.
  - **Inline images**: ImageAddon now loaded — handles iTerm2 (OSC 1337) and Sixel protocols for opencode's image drag-and-drop feature.
  - **Rapid output**: 5ms data coalescing + flow control (100K char high watermark) handle opencode's fast code generation output without buffer overflow.
  - **Large scrollback**: 100K lines + 5MB ring buffer handle extended agent sessions with extensive tool output.
  - **Clickable URLs**: WebLinksAddon detects URLs in opencode output (PR links, docs, file paths).
  - **GPU rendering**: WebGL addon handles rapid full-screen redraws from opencode's TUI layout updates.

### Design decisions
- **`COLORTERM=truecolor` over terminal type change**: The terminal type (`TERM=xterm-256color`) stays unchanged because many programs and terminfo databases expect it. `COLORTERM=truecolor` is the standard env var that applications check specifically for 24-bit color capability. Both modern terminal emulators (Ghostty, WezTerm, Kitty) and TUI frameworks (opencode, Charm/Bubble Tea, Ink) check `COLORTERM` independently of `TERM`.
- **Image addon added**: Unlike Issue #125 (Claude Code) which concluded "no image addon needed", opencode explicitly supports image drag-and-drop into the terminal prompt. The addon is small (~30KB minified) and loaded in a try/catch, so it adds negligible overhead and doesn't affect terminals that don't use image protocols.
- **`cursorStyle: "bar"` over default "block"**: Bar cursor matches opencode's default and is the more common cursor style in modern code editors (VS Code, Cursor). The change affects all terminals, not just opencode, but bar cursor is universally appropriate for coding contexts.
- **No separate `LANG`/`LC_ALL` injection**: These locale env vars are inherited from `process.env` (the Bun server's environment). On macOS, they default to `en_US.UTF-8` which is correct for Unicode support. Explicitly setting them could override intentional locale customization by the user.
